			* consisting of 5 coils of silk rope (50’ each); 10 flasks of oil; 2 dozen spikes; 4 quivers with 20 arrows each; 4 quivers with 12 crossbow bolts each; 4 bundles of firewood; 2 grappling hooks; 12 pieces of chalk; a bag of marbles; 6 empty sacks; 4 leather scroll cases; 12 waterskins
			* Books: the Courtship of Julius the Exarch, Great Villains of Archontos, part II: Kegfiller the Proedros, the Twelve Labors of Arden, and On Friends and Enemies.
			* Gyrde’s Spell Book: Erase, hold portal, magic missile, push, read magic, run, shield, sleep, unseen servant; bind, continual light, darkness 15’ radius, detect invisibility, locate object, shatter; dispel magic, fireball, lightning bolt, suggestion; dig

The following members of the Bad Neighbors are present here: Diomedes, Cyricus, and Gyrde.
* Recommend mid or high level when encountered here.

4 non-classed human bearers: SZ M; AL LN; AC 9; MV 120’; HD 1; HP 8, 6, 5, 3; #AT 1; Dmg 1-4 (dagger).

### 6-130: Tomb of Lucius Cornelius Scriptor: Antechamber

* A permanent illusion conceals the entrance from the chasm.
* This is the antechamber to the tomb of Lucius Cornelius Scriptor, protonotarius (chief administrative officer) of the great archon, Marius Tricotor (6-154).
	* The floor features a 15’x5’ mosaic of an Archontean face, oriented such that the top of the head is by the door to 6-131.
		* The face mosaic is remarkably detailed, with some tesserae shaped specially to fit their purpose, the lined face of a man (Lucius Cornelius Scriptor) in his 50’s or 60’s, with the typical Roman nose of the Archontean aristocracy, close-cropped hair, and several warts by his nose.
		* A magic mouth speaks (Mithric) if the mosaic is touched, the lips moving, repeating every 5 rounds.
			* Hail, Friend! Lucius the scriptor, of the Cornelius clan, rests within, happily surrounded by the ghosts of his ancestors. Let his service to unconquered Marius Tricotor, archon and imperator, stand as a record to his fidelity and service to Archontos. Lucius is tired. Importune him no more. Rather, let him rest!
	* A dozen 4’-tall basalt pillars line the south and west walls, topped with life-sized, lifelike, painted, marble busts of men and women (5 lbs, 200 gp to the Krakteros clan).  Each has a name scratched into the bottom.
		* 7 men and 5 women of the Cornelius clan, relatives of Lucius Scriptor.
			* Licinia Septima; Sixtus the Praetor; Junius the younger, Cornelia of the collegium, Mendax the Outcast, etc.. 
			* (4d6 under Int) Cornelian clan largely died out 500 years ago, with its remaining members subsumed into the Krakteros (one of the Five Families).
		* The bust of Mendax the Outcast s far more generic and stylized than the others (lacking crows-feet, moles, small scars, and other features that render the remaining busts so lifelike).
			* An internal compartment holds the key to the secret door to 6-133.
			* Stone-cunning or trap-finding might notice the weight is off.
	* Both doors are stone and locked (keys long gone).
	* Secret Door (south, -15% to pick, difficult): han unusual x-shaped keyhole (key inside the the bust of Mendax the Outcast).

### 6-131: Trapped Corridor

* The wooden door visible at the end of the long, narrow corridor is a false door.
	* If opened, a stone block drops from the ceiling by the real door to 6-130, completely blocking the corridor except for a 6” gap.
	* Detection (dwarves, 60%; thieves, +5% to spot but -10% disarm).

### 6-132: False Floor

* The north, south, and west walls of this chamber are painted with vibrant scenes of common persons and soldiers bringing treasures and tributes before a seated man depicted on the east wall.
* The center of the floor is painted with another image of Lucius Cornelius (not a mosaic, as in 6-130).
	* Just east of the image of Lucius Cornelius is an 8’x3’x4’ sarcophagus.
	* The floor is an illusion covering a 30’-deep pit. Only the ‘sarcophagus’ is real, the carved tip of a 30’-tall pillar.
		* The fall deals 3d6.  3d6 under DEX or hit sparse spikes (2d4).
		* Two hungry ghouls are also marooned in the pit.
		* The corpse of a half-elf magic user/thief rests on the floor of the pit.
			* Boots of elvenkind, belt pouch (four pearls (100 gp each), a scroll (extension I, fly), well-tooled gloves of red leather (one of which has a bag of holding (smallest capacity) sewn into its liner).
				* Spellbook (in glove-bag): charm person, comprehend languages, detect magic, feather fall, floating disk, hold portal, jump, light, read magic, shield, shocking grasp, spider climb; audible glamer, darkness 15’ radius, detect invisibility, invisibility, knock, levitate, mirror image, pyrotechnics, rope trick, strength, wizard lock; blink, dispel magic, fly, invisibility 10’ radius, protection from normal missiles, slow; charm monster, extension I, fire trap, mnemonic enhancement, polymorph other, remove curse.

2 ghouls: SZ M; AL CE; AC 6; MV 90’; HD 2; HP 14, 12; #AT 3; Dmg 1-3/1-3/1-6. Special attacks: paralysis. Special defenses: immune to sleep and charm.

### 6-133: False Tomb of the Scriptor

* A huge sarcophagus (15’ x 5’ x 5’) sits in the center of this room.
	* The stone cover carving depicts Lucius Cornelius in the elaborate ceremonial attire of an imperial official.  Open doors check to remove.
	* The interior appears solid gold studded with precious and semiprecious stones
		* Actually fool’s gold and colored glass (3d6 under INT to notice).
		* A wrapped skeleton (not Lucius Cornelius) lies in state with a silver-and-ruby medallion of thought projection prominently displayed on its chest.
			* Disturbing it causes a ghostly spirit to follow the defiler, moaning dire but wordless imprecations and making their life miserable (-25% reaction rolls, hard to sneak, etc), until an exorcism spell is cast.
* Around the sarcophagus are a dozen pieces of large, gilt furniture, some stacked on top of each other.
	* 4 occasional tables, a delicate canopied bed, a set of campaigning furniture, 6 dining chairs. All is gilt (125 gp if stripped) and purely ceremonial.
	* By the west wall are a huge writing desk (6’ tall, 8’ wide) and a large scroll cabinet.
		* Both are formed of ivory-inlaid teakwood, functional and extremely valuable (1,500 gp and 300 gp respectively; 4d6 under INT to disassemble).
			* 4 scrolls in the case: a cursed scroll; the Lay of Marius Invictus, by Lucius Cornelius Scriptor (books); a scroll of protection from possession; and the Secreta Secretorum (books).
	* Two large stone chests lie against the south side of the sarcophagus.
		* One contains 22,451 cp, the other contains 18,978 cp.
* Ten half-round stone warriors line the walls of the chamber; they take the form of Archontean legionaries.
	* Between the statues the walls are painted with vibrant frescoes of mundane Archontean administration, with one dark-haired man (Lucius Cornelius) centered.
		* On the south wall, it shows Lucius Cornelius sitting by a figure in sumptuous purple robes with a gold circlet and numerous gaudy pieces of jewelry.  Inscription (Mithric): “Thus the Scriptor aided the glorious Marius Tricotor in the acquisition and distribution of wealth.” 
			* This fresco is a red herring.  Anyone who knows about Marius Tricotor will  recognize Marius was a simple soldier first and always, and eschewed finery and acclaim.
* Secret Door (west wall of corridor, just outside the room proper): difficult to locate (1 in 8), no opening mechanism, can be shattered by 10 damage.

### 6-134: Stone Golem

* At the west end of this narrow chamber stands a stone golem, carved to resemble an Archontean legionary.
	* It activates when any living being ventures 20’ west of the door to 6-133.
	* It pursues intruders into 6-133 and 6-130. 
* Secret Door (south): leads to the true tomb of Lucius Cornelius.  Not made to be reopened, must be broken (15 HP damage).

1 stone golem: SZ L; AL N; AC 5; MV 60’; HD 14; HP 60; #AT 1; Dmg 3-24. Special attacks: slow once every other round. Special defenses: +2 or better weapons to hit; immune to most magic.

### 6-135: Tomb of Lucius Cornelius Scriptor

* In contrast to the grandeur of the false tomb, the true tomb of Lucius Cornelius is spartan.
	* A fresco covers the south wall in which Lucius Cornelius (recognizable by the warts near his nose, see 6-130), in a simple white tunic, stands next to Marius, himself dressed as a simple legionary, carrying a red-handled gladius.
	* Inscription (Mithric): “Lucius and Marius. Friends in life, friends in death. In simplicity there is truth.” 
* A sarcophagus lies against the west wall, undecorated save for the inscription “Lucius Cornelius, friend of Marius.”  (open doors to remove lid)
	* Inside is an alabaster urn (50 gp) that holds the ashes of Lucius Cornelius, as well as a carpet of 5,429 ancient silver pennies and 1,387 ancient gold solidi.
		* Amongst the coins are an ioun stone (pale lavender) and a silver circlet (helm of comprehend languages and read magic).
		* Ashes of Lucius Cornelius: if disturbed (or scattered), the defiler is geased to bring the bodies of 10 heqeti to the tomb of Marius Tricotor (6-154).
* A small bookshelf) and an armor rack occupy the east wall.
	* The bookshelf contains five items:
		* The Deeds of Marius Tricotor, by Lucius Cornelius Scriptor (books)
		* The Value of Mud, by Herodian the Blessed (books)
		* The Ineffable Apprehension of Thoth (a tome of clear thought)
		* Vul Speaks (books)
		* A bifolium with the addresses and clearly annotated locations of two Thothian teleportation rings (6-141 and 4-171).
	* The armor rack contains:
		* A battered suit of Archontean legionary armor with scorch marks on the breastplate (armor of Marius, new).
			* A reader of the Deeds of Marius Tricotor will recognize the scorches.
		* A gladius in a simple wooden sheath with a grip wrapped in red linen (sword of Marius, new).
	* GM: Possession of the sword and the armor is necessary to activate certain effects in the tomb of Marius Tricotor (6-154).

### 6-136: Cold Crossroads

* The walls of this crossroads chamber are thickly carved with floral bas-reliefs.
	* Interspersed among the flora are a dozen figures of rudishva. 
* The air is cool (45-degrees F).
* The floor is littered with brittle and desiccated bits of discarded adventuring gear.
* The south door (locked) is rimmed with frost and is extremely cold to the touch.
	* The lock is jammed with ice, and he door frozen shut (bend bars to force).
	* The varumani (6-5) have nailed up a sign: (Varumani, i.e. Mithric with Glyphik influences), “Entrance Forbidden! This means you!”

## Level 6: 137 - 142 (Ice Chambers)

* The walls, floors and ceilings of most of the areas south of the troll lift (6-5) are bone cold (-20 F) and covered with nearly a foot of snow and ice.
	* Difficult terrain (+1x) and -1 to all rolls, from snow and slippery ice.
	* Crunchy snow makes silent movement difficult.
	* 1d6 hp / Turn lost without suitable warmth, clothing, etc (2d6kh1 for Small).
* The frost mother bound to 6-140 is the source of these environmental conditions.
	* If slain, each room will gradually thaw over 2d6 days, revealing things concealed.

### 6-137: Frozen Lounge

* This chamber is bone cold and covered in almost a foot of snow and ice.
	* Numerous footprints dot the snow, and a rough path leads from the chamber to both 6-136 and 6-140.
* 3 frost ghouls, reanimated from slain adventurers, wait patiently for new victims to bring to the frost mother in 6-140. 
	* Combat in 6-140 brings them at a lope on the round indicated at 6-140.

After the Ice has Thawed
* No surviving wall decorations, but a beautiful shallow pool fills the center.
	* The bottom of the pool (filled with melting ice) is inlaid with 350 semi-precious stones (10 gp each, chip out 5 / Turn).
* A corpse of an Archontean legionary officer (Justinus) in the northwest corner.
	* Chain mail, Archontean gladius, a potion of heroism, a purse (35 ancient silver pennies, 2 parchment notes).
		* Note 1 (seal broken, Archontean): “To kentarch Justinus, from Guivrel, advisor to Archon Adrienic. Deliver this writ to the thief and deserter Pollitt. If possible, ensure his peaceful return to Adrienic’s seat of governance by the Hall of Forty Pillars. If not possible, you are empowered to deal with him by any means necessary.”
			* GM Note: these are the legionary’s orders
			* Guivrel, see 5-11; for the Hall of Forty Pillars, see 5-6. 
		* Note 2 (sealed, Archontean): “Comrade Pollitt. Your hairy allies have been defeated. Return to the archon with the items you have stolen or face our wrath. (signed) Lankios.”
			* GM Note: still sealed; Justinus was slain by Pollitt before he could deliver it.
			* Identical to the writ on Pollitt’s body in 6-140. 

3 frost ghouls (see new monsters): SZ M; AL NE; AC 8; MV 120’; HD 3; HP 20, 18, 16; #AT 1; Dmg 1-8. Special attacks: cold aura (5', 1 hp/rnd). Special defenses: immune to cold; turned as wights.
* A silver cup with garnets (175 gp)
* A pouch filled with copper shavings (35 gp)
* A long sword +1

### 6-138: Frozen Campsite

* This chamber is covered with a foot of snow and ice.
	* 3 frost ghouls reside here.  Their tracks lead west to 6-140.

After the Ice has Thawed
* The campsite of Pollitt the Sorcerer is revealed: an improvised fire ring and small stack of firewood.
	* A couple of saddlebags
		* Saddlebag #1: silk clothing in various ancient styles and wild colors (250 gp); a token of Arden (AV items); a guard cap (new); and 5 empty iron scroll cases.
		* Saddlebag #2: 12 pieces of ancient pottery looted from tombs in 5-18 to 5-24.
			* Ten of the pieces (125 gp each).
			* One shows a key scene from the Tale of Larel One-Eye and the Legionary (AV books) (250 gp).
			* One shows Marius the archon, dressed as a common legionary, being named as one of the Twenty Worthies of Archontos by a grateful emperor (250 gp).
	* The body of Hector, Pollitt’s apprentice, throat cut.
		* A wand of frost (4 charges); an iron key (to SL8-1)
		* A parchment draft of a letter Hector never delivered (Archontean).
			* Numerous erasures and lined out words.
			* ‘Hector, humble scribe to Pollitt the Mighty, to Lord Strategos Lankios, peace and friendship. Your lordship, I do not know how to best phrase what must be said in this missive, so I will eschew the usual pleasantries and move directly to the point. You cannot trust Guivrel. She has been corrupted by that ring, which my master Pollitt found in the Hall of Forty Pillars and gave to her as a gift. It is cursed! Cursed, I tell you! Pollitt knew it well, which is why he allowed it to pass from his hands to your Guivrel. The ring changes a person’s thoughts, rendering the victim cruel, calculating, and enamored of treachery. I beg of you to force Guivrel to surrender the ring, and then to destroy it. Only then might she return to her usual good-natured self. Please take these words as they are intended: humble advice from a friend to a powerful lord.’
				* GM Note: a clue to the fate of Lankios, Guivrel and Kaitor (5-11), as well as to the nature of Pollitt (6-140).

3 frost ghouls (see new monsters): SZ M; AL NE; AC 8; MV 120’; HD 3; HP 20, 18, 16; #AT 1; Dmg 1-8. Special attacks: cold aura. Special defenses: immune to cold; turned as wights.

### 6-139: Frozen Storeroom

* An ice- and snow-filled room, with over a dozen lumps and humps ranging from 2” to 5” in height, hindering movement.
	* The humps are the snow-covered boxes, barrels, and kegs.
	* A 5’-diameter hole on the east wall leads to natural tunnels and 6-125 and 6-127.
	* Tracks in the snow lead from the hole to the hallway to 6-140; spatters of relatively fresh blood dot the snow along the path.
* 3 frost ghouls inhabit this chamber.
	* They lope to the aid of the frost mother if combat breaks out in 6-140.

After the Ice has Thawed
* A dozen wooden boxes, four very large barrels, and a dozen smaller kegs become visible.
	* The liquids in the kegs and barrels are all potable, but quite unappealing and valueless (being frozen a long time).
	* Amongst the usable items in the boxes: a box of several hundred nails; a set of surveying instruments (50 gp); 2 50’-coils of rope (now weakened by the cold and wet; break if more than 50 lb weight placed on them); a set of 40 glass marbles; a set of ivory and jet Archontean chess figures (250 gp); and 12 iron spikes.

3 frost ghouls (see new monsters): SZ M; AL NE; AC 8; MV 120’; HD 3; HP 20, 18, 16; #AT 1; Dmg 1-8. Special attacks: cold aura. Special defenses: immune to cold; turned as wights.

### 6-140: Chamber of the Frost Mother

* This dark and frigid chamber is the source of the ice and cold that dominates the surrounding caves, for a terrible frost mother is bound to this chamber.
* The entire room is covered with a foot of snow over several more inches of ice.
	* Six corpses lie half-buried among the crunchy snow.
	* A dais in the northwest corner, topped with a throne flanked by spiral-carved stone columns, is buried under a dramatic snow mound.
		* Atop it sits a woman apparently carved of snow, with coal black eyes.
			* Always appears as a snow doppelganger of the viewer's mother.
			* She will exhale a cone of cold and the corpses rise as frost ghouls.
			* She cannot be reasoned with, and fights to the bitter end.
			* She cannot leave the chamber.
			* She regenerates 1 hp / Turn while surrounded by snow and ice.
			* If combat lasts > 3 rounds, frost ghouls start arriving from 6-137 (round 8), 6-138 (round 4) and 6-139 (round 6).

Background
* The frost mother was summoned by the Archontean sorcerer, Pollitt, during the ill-fated imperial effort to reclaim the halls 250 years ago.
* The mage’s frozen body has lain under the snow at the foot of the throne for centuries, but the frost mother is unable to return to the para-elemental plane of ice.
* Marooned and increasingly unstable, she has created an environment suited to her native plane and has populated it with the frost ghouls created from the corpses of those unfortunates who have died at her hands. 

After the Ice has Thawed
* The wall frescoes on the walls are illegible, but a fine floor mosaic remains.
	* It shows an authoritative-looking Archontean dressed in ordinary legionary attire and identified as “Marius” receiving the homage of a half-dozen warriors and officials, all dressed in glittering finery.
* The corpse of Pollitt the Summoner and a carelessly incomplete summoning pentagram before the throne.
	* Ring of protection +2; a jar of stone salve (3 doses); a mother-of-pearl box decorated with scenes from the tales of Larel One-Eye (375 gp); a bowl of controlling water elementals; a dagger +2; a silver ankh-key; yellow and green glass activation squares
	* A tightly wrapped, once-sealed parchment writ (Archontean): “Comrade Pollitt. Your hairy allies have been defeated. Return to the archon with the items you have stolen or face our wrath. (signed) Lankios.”
	* Pollitt’s spell book has been mostly destroyed by the cold
		* Still legible: conjure elemental, dolor, monster summoning III, and geas.

GM Notes: Pollitt abandoned his post in Adrienic's command (5-18), the imperial archon sent 250 years ago to recover the halls, and stole the bowl of controlling water elementals. The note is from Lankios, who still lives as a hermit (1-6).

6 frost ghouls: SZ M; AL NE; AC 8; MV 120’; HD 3; HP 22, 20, 19, 18, 17, 16; #AT 1; Dmg 1-8. Special attacks: cold aura. Special defenses: immune to cold; turned as wights.
* 39 sp, 58 gp, 23 pp; 13 ancient silver pennies, 3 octagonal platinum coins; an aquamarine (100 gp), a peridot (125 gp); a scroll of fireball; and a spear +2 w/ ivory-capped haft.

def 12, atk 15
0 / 22
0 / 20
0 / 19
0 / 18
0 / 17
0 / 16

1 frost mother: SZ M; AL NE; AC 2; MV 60’; HD 8; HP 59; #AT 3 (spit ice slivers, 40'); Dmg 1-4/1-4/1-4; MR 10%. Special attacks: cold aura (10', 1d3 / round); cone of cold (2/day, 8d4+8); ice storm (2/day; sleet form); create ice ghouls from slain (1d6 rounds). Special defenses: +2 or better weapons to hit; immune to cold; regenerate 1 HP/ Turn in cold environments, +2 dmg per die from fire/heat.
* Always appears as a snow doppelganger of the viewer's mother.

X / 59, def 18, atk 19

reinforcements 2 / 3


### 6-141: The Lady’s Asylum

* The ubiquitous snow and ice covers the eastern half of this 20’-tall chamber.
* The west wall is fully occupied by an enormous sculpture of a human woman's face.
	* 15' high, carved in 3/4 relief.  A young, beautiful woman with elaborate ancient archontean hair, a benign smile.  Painted w/ vibrant olive skin, black hair, blue eyes, yellow necklace.
		* Carved in the likeness of Lady Clementia, wife of Marius.  Represents the idealized virtues expected of a noblewoman, including mercy and protection.
	* Warmth radiates from her visage, and west of the entrance is free of snow and ice. 
		* 20' around the face is under Protection from Evil and kept warm.  Frost ghouls will not approach.
		* Orally beseeching her assistance grants a Protection from Evil spell for 1 hour.
			* If invoked by name (Clementia), lasts an entire day.
			* One may receive the Lady’s blessing once per month. 
	* Deeply cut inscriptions in Mithric fill the southwest and northwest walls.
		* 2' tall, filled with gold (100 gp, 2 hours to extract).  Removal breaks the aura of protection.
		* NW
			* Raised to the purple
			* Beside the unconquered one,
			* Her clemency echoes
			* The sweetness of her name
		* SW
			* Let those in need of mercy,
			* Those seeking a mother’s breast,
			* Those in search of protection,
			* Beseech her benign goodwill

After the Ice has Thawed
* The Thothian teleporation ring under the ice on the east side of the room is revealed (BL-GR-BK-WH-RE-YE).
	* No glass activation squares are present.

### 6-142: Fountain of Marius

* The surfaces of this 20’-tall chamber are covered in inches of snow and ice.
	* Around the fountain is a 3’ space without snow or frost.
* An unfrozen marble pool, 30’ long, 5’ wide, 4' tall, occupies the center of the chamber, bookended by two 20’ legionary statues.
	* Each statue holds a gladius in one hand and an olifant-style drinking horn over the trough in the other.  Cold, clear water pours from the horns to fill the trough.
	* Carved from basalt, and quite lifelike.  Archaic, but distinct, facial features, articulated splint mail.
	* If the Oath of Loyalty to the Emperor (hidden under ice on the wall) is recited, drinking the water acts as a potion of super-heroism and heals 2d6, once per month.
	* Drinking without reciting the oath tastes bitter and has no effect, and the four stone statues animate and attack
* Four 8’-tall statues of Archontean legionaries stand against the slanted walls of the chamber.

After the Ice has Thawed
* North wall: a 2’-tall inscription (Mithric) filled with gold (100 gp, 2 hours to pry out)
	* Imperator! With faith and strength I uphold your authority and obey your rightful commands. Imperator!
		* Reciting this oath here activates the beneficial effects of the fountain. 
* Secret Door (southeast, beside stone legionary): invisible under snow and ice. Once thawed, detect normally. Opens by simply pushing a 4’-square panel inwards.

4 stone legionaries, as Archontean animated constructs - spearmen (see new monsters): SZ M; AL N; AC 2; MV 60’; HD 6; HP 45, 40, 35, 33; #AT 1; Dmg 5-10; MR 25%. Special defenses: immune to elemental magic, poison, and mind-affecting spells; +1 or better weapons to hit; half damage from slashing or piercing weapons.


## Level 6: 143 - 168

### 6-143: Spillway from the Drowned Canyon (SL6-25)

* This passage allows overflow water from the dam at the east end of the Drowned Canyon (SL6-25) to pour into the Great Chasm (6-108).
	* For most of its length, the spillway is 40’ wide, 4’ tall, and semicircular, with natural stone walls, but a flat, smoothed granite floor, slippery with moss in many places.
	* 150’ from the chasm, the spillway changes direction and narrows to a 10’-diameter tube that extends to the edge of the chasm, where water running through it forms a steady waterfall (6-6a).
	* The pitch is gentle, 20 degrees in the wider part, 25 degrees in the narrower section. A cautious party should have little trouble traversing the spillway.
	* 50’ west of where the narrow section widens out, a breach in the roof of the spillway leads to a 5’ tunnel snaking north and west to 6-159.

### 6-144: Stairs Down to SL13-27 (Lost Chambers of Arden)

* The secret door in 6-142 leads to a 4’-wide passage and stairs down 350’ to SL13-27.
	* It is impossible to open from the east side until 6-142 is thawed.

### 6-145: Shrine to Marius

* The stone door is locked, but easy to pick (+5%).
* This was the public shrine to the great archon, Marius Tricotor.
	* It portrays Marius like an Archontean aristocrat, consumed with desire for status and appropriate honor. Those familiar with Marius will know his usual depiction as a man of simplicity who eschewed formality and luxury.
* The chamber is 20’ tall and barrel vaulted.
	* The floors and ceilings are painted imperial purple.  All statues are painted to resemble actual flesh, clothing, and equipment.
	* The entire room detects of magic. 
	* A dais (15’ long, 10’ wide, 5’ tall) dominates the center of the room. Behind it is a 15’ statue of Marius Tricotor and his adoring secretary, Lucius Cornelius.
		* A short stair leads up on the south end to a top sheathed in blue marble.
		* When the top is touched, a magic mouth speaks from the central statue.
			* (Mithric) “I am Marius Tricotor the Great. My nobility was recognized early in my career, and I received the promotions I deserved. Here, at Arden Vul, I received the homage of the troll thegn and devised and executed the plan that drove back the hopping hordes of the slimy dwellers in the dark. For this I received appropriate honors and ruled as archon, enjoying the friendship of the Emperor himself. I am truly worthy to be listed among the Twenty. My loyal friend, Lucius Cornelius, wrote the true account of my deeds and chose to entomb himself nearby.”
			* GM Note: ‘the Twenty’ refers to the Worthies of the Archontean Empire.
		* The main statue of Marius stands with right arm outstretched, cloaked in a purple-trimmed white toga draped to leave the right shoulder bare.
			* His visage is stylized and generic; unlined, unblemished, smiling thinly.
			* He wears a heavy gold circlet studded with red gems and 3 thick gold rings.  Cradled in his left arm is a pair of fasces. Sheathed by his right side is a legionary gladius.
				* The rings, short sword, and toga are removable, but non-valuable, painted, sculptural items.
			* Inscribed on the south side of the pediment (Mithric): “the Great Archon, Marius Tricotor.”
		* A man kneels next to him, looking up with awe at Marius.
			* A smaller inscription on the east side: “Lucius Cornelius, scribe and confidant, recipient of the relics of the great man.” ( Lucius Cornelius’s tomb is at 6-135)
			* Lucius Cornelius is less elaborate, without removable garb.
			* The head is hollow, removable by twisting.
				* Inside is a folded parchment (Mithric): “Lucius Cornelius received the armor and sword of Marius Tricotor, and added them to his collection. Now they are gone, hidden in the scriptor’s tomb, which that suspicious ingrate has concealed from all.” (see 6-135)
	* Six more 10’ sculptures line the walls, each standing on a 2’ semicircular dais.
		* The six groupings that line the wall depict stages of Marius' career.
			* In each Marius and other figures appears in a highly idealized way.
		* From the southeast corner, the sculptural scenes depict:
			* 1) Marius the Legionary: a young man, attired as a common legionary, standing at attention.
				* The only acknowledgement that Marius was a commoner who rose through the ranks (instead of the mythmaking of the rest of the iconography).
			* 2) Marius the Kentarch: uniformed as a commander of 100 men, pointing with his javelin towards an imagined enemy.
			* 3) Marius in ceremonial armor receiving the fealty of the troll thegn: extending his left hand which a writhing, skinny varumani kisses humbly.
			* 4) Marius Invictus, trampling the heqeti: in ceremonial armor and holding a baton of office, steps on the neck of a heqeti hopper. 
			* 5) Marius the Archon: dressed in elaborate courtier’s garb, rendering judgment on a kneeling man
			* 6) Marius and the Emperor, both dressed resplendently: bows slightly before the emperor, who places a hand of friendship on his shoulder.
	* Secret Door (ceiling): a circular door, 10’ in diameter, in the ceiling.
		* Opens when one gold ring on the central statue’s hand is twisted. Leads to a broad but low (4’-tall) passage to 6-146.

* If the chamber door is left open, the inhabitants of 6-157 will investigate in 4 rounds.

* GM Note: The broad outline of Marius’s career is accurately told here. It is the insistence on Marius’s natural nobility and typically aristocratic predilection for deference and honor that deviates from reality.

### 6-146: Ceiling Bolt Hole

* This chamber is only 4’ tall and is rough-carved from the rock, one of the few navigable routes between the eastern portion of Level 6 and the tomb of Marius Tricotor (6-154).
	* A 10’-diameter hole in the floor leads to the ceiling of the corridor between 6-148 and 6-154.
	* The southward tunnel ends in a 10’-diameter circular hatch into the ceiling of 6-145.
	* A dry and cracked leather haversack lies on the floor of the chamber
		* Coil of silk rope, an ancient terra cotta plaque stamped with an image of the archon, Marius Tricotor (15 gp).

### 6-147: Sub-Archon’s Quarters

* An imperial sub-archon oversaw an official honor guard for Marius Tricotor’s tomb (6-154) from this location.
	* The sub-archon and his men swore binding oaths to protect the tomb with their lives, and so the last unit of these guards remains at its post.
	* The door is locked (+10% to pick); the one key lies within.
* The chamber is painted sky blue, with green laurel wreaths (an imperial symbol) at 3’ intervals.
	* A 5’-tall writing desk stands at the center of the room.
	* To the west is a wooden screen, behind which is a cot, wardrobe, and armor stand.
		* Wardrobe: badly decayed wool and linen clothing, 2 usable yellow silk surcoats with the letters MI embroidered on front and back (MI = Marius Invictus).
		* Armor stand: yellow-died legionary banded mail +1, a short sword +2, and a bundle of 4 javelins of piercing. 
	* To the east is a long, rectangular table on which are tacked some maps.
		* The maps on the table include the following: 1) a map of Burdock’s Valley; 2) a map of the city of Arden Vul; and 3) a map of the environs of the Tomb of Marius Tricotor (areas 6-5, 6-136 to 6-142, and 6-145 to 6-148). 
	* A narrow table on the north wall holds some symbolic objects.

### 6-148: Barracks Chamber

* The walls are sky-blue, with yellow helmets painted over the blue every 3’.
	* The sleepless guardsmen pushed the 12 rotting wooden bunkbeds to the south. 
		* Among the debris is a rotting chest: 1,311 ancient silver pennies, a scroll of extension II, a wand of frost (12 charges).
* Thanks to their eternal oath, the elite guard still stands watch in the guardsmen’s former barracks as oathbound knights (new).
	* Dressed in yellow-died banded mail and tattered yellow surcoats with the MI insignia (see 6-147). 
	* They stand quietly, ready to repel desecrators of the tomb of Marius Tricotor (6-154) or the areas of east of the tomb.  They confront anyone who opens the door from 6-154 or who descends from the hole to 6-146.
		* Intruders have only a couple of rounds to convince them (in Mithric) that their purpose does not involve disrespect, plunder, or desecration.
		* They don't attack anyone who presents a true artifact of Marius (e.g., his sword or armor from 6-135).
		* If the talismans of their oaths (see 6-149), they crumble into dust.

8 oathbound knights (see new monsters): SZ M; AL LN; AC 5; MV 90’; HD 6; HP 47, 44, 43, 42, 41, 40, 39, 37; #AT 3/2; Dmg 3-9 (broadsword), 3-6 (horseman’s flail), 1-4 (light crossbow); 
MR 25%. Special attacks: +1 to hit, +1 damage. Special defenses: +1 or better weapons to hit. Possessions: chain mail; broadsword; light flail; light crossbow, 20 quarrels.

Publius Lanlius, the oathbound knight-commander (see new monsters): SZ M; AL LN; AC 3; MV 90’; HD 9; HP 63; #AT 3/2; Dmg 5-12 (long sword +3); MR 25%. Special attacks: +1 
to hit, +1 damage. Special defenses: +1 or better weapons to hit.
* Possessions: chain mail +2; long sword +3, key to 6-149, ring of Marius (new).
* Folded parchment w/ address of Thothian teleportation ring at SL4-49 (black - red - yellow-green-blue-white).

### 6-149: Repository of the Oaths

* Secret Door (from hallway, locked, -5% to pick): key held by the oathbound commander (6-148).
* This long, barrel-vaulted room has a 20’ ceiling, with ceiling and walls painted sunflower yellow.
	* Words (Mithric) in bold black paint on the east and west walls: Discipline, Order, Loyalty, Fidelity, and Service.
	* Stone benches fill the northern two-thirds of the chamber.
	* At the south end is an obsidian shrine on a dais 2’ tall, 10’ wide, and 8’ across.
		* The north edge of the platform contains an apparently solid 5’ cube of obsidian.
			* Each side is inscribed and filled with silver (Mithric): “The Archon’s Heart is Worthy of Service.”
			* The top also has an 3/4” silver-lined indentation.
			* If the ring of Marius (new, borne by the commander in 6-148) is inserted, the obsidian cube slides back, revealing a 1’-square hole in the platform holding the the mummified heart of Marius, wrapped in linen.
				* A parchment tag on the wrap reads (Mithric): “This is the Heart of Marius Tricotor, taken from his body when the archon died.”
		* Behind the cube, at the platform's rear is a half pillar, 3’ in diameter and 5’ high.
			* On top is a finely carved, hyper-realistic marble bust of Marius Tricotor.
				* Attached to the bust by string are nine small talismans.
					* These are tokens of the oaths sworn by the oathbound knights (6-148); if destroyed, the corresponding knight crumbles to dust.
					* Ordinary knight talismans: a lock of hair; a cameo with a man’s head; a small knife; a scrap of parchment with the name “Gnaeus” on it; a terra cotta icon of Marius Tricotor; a cheap necklace of copper and glass (5 gp); a small vial with dried blood; and another small vial with a desiccated human finger (pinky) in it.
					* Commander’s talisman: gold amulet set with carnelians (375 gp).

### 6-150: Empty Guardpost

* A few benches, a table, and ancient pewter mugs are all that remain of this guard post.
* A faded fresco on the south wall shows a yellow-clad legionary under the motto (Mithric): “By our oath we show our service to Emperor and Archon!”

### 6-151: Robing Room

* This 15’-tall room is painted bright yellow and studded with pegs for hanging clothes.
	* A few shreds of yellow silk hang from a few of the pegs.
	* Over the exit to the south is a faded slogan in yellow paint (Mithric): “Fidelity to our Lord Marius.”
* GM Note: Imperial custodians of the tomb of Marius Tricotor always wore a yellow surcoat with the initials “MI” (Marius Invictus); those arriving from what are now the Flooded Vaults (Sub-Level 7) stopped here to dress. 

### 6-152: Stairs to Surface (AV-27)

* This narrow (5’-wide), circular staircase wends its way upward  1,200’ to a secret door in the basement of the Carrion Tower of the Donjon in the Ruined City (AV-27).

### 6-153: Stairs and Corridor to SL7-6

* A set of stairs descends briefly before turning into a corridor west, which then ascends 250’ over many short staircases to the Flooded Vaults (SL7-6).

### 6-154: Tomb of Marius Tricotor

* One of the legendary lost locations of the Halls, isolated from most traffic for a millennium since the passage to 6-157 collapsed.
* The chamber is 30’ tall and barrel vaulted.
	* Eight statues (10’ tall) of legionaries stand along the east and west walls. 
	* To the south a 10’-wide passage leads south, only to end in a cave-in. 
	* At the north edge of the chamber is a colossal carved head of Marius Tricotor; 15’ tall, 6’ in diameter and mounted on a 5’-square pedestal.
		* The base of the pedestal carries an inscription in Mithric.
		* It is carved of marble in elaborate detail, down to the last hair, wrinkle, and blemish, showing a man of late middle age, with close cropped hair, a broken Roman nose, pursed lips, and sharp, penetrating eyes made of  basalt chips.
		* Approaching within 5’ triggers a magic mouth that intones (Mithric):
			* “Only those who know me well may summon me to their side. Restore those objects that symbolize my nature, and I shall return to aid you in your need. Choose poorly, and your ignorance and lack of faith shall be punished!”
		* Placing the suitable objects on the four basalt platforms summons the spirit of Marius Tricotor to inhabit his head for 4-6 days (see below).
	* Down the center are four basalt platforms, each 5’ long, 10’ wide, and 3’ tall.
		* The sides of each platform are inscribed with one of Marius' virtues in gold filled (Mithric) letters.
		* On top of each platform is an 8’-tall, marble half-statue of Marius: torso, arms, hands, and head.
			* Each ‘statue’ has indentations in the same locations: skull (10” diameter), eyes (4” ovals), and chest (12” diameter).
			* If any incorrect item (e.g. ‘false’ items from 6-145) is placed on any of the half-statues, 2 stone legionaries per wrong object animate and attack.

Virtue Distinctiveness Solution
* 1) Fidelity
	* The statues’ arms are outstretched and the fingers of both its hands are open and outstretched.
		* Roll 4d6 under INT to notice wear on the right ring finger. 
	* Place the ring of Marius (currently in 6-148) on any of Marius’s fingers. 
* 2) Protection
	* Hands are held at the torso's waist, fingers of both are closed as if to grip something.
	* Those who wear armor can roll 4d6 under INT to notice wear marks where the straps to attach armor should be. 
	* Attach the armor of Marius (6-135) on the torso.
* 3) Vengeance
	* The torso is slightly swiveled and the left arm is thrust forward. The fingers of both hands are closed as if to grip something.
	* Any sword-wielding PC may roll 4d6 under INT to detect wear marks in the right hand. 
	* Place the sword of Marius (6-135) in the left hand.
* 4) Nobility
	* Both arms are folded behind the torso’s back.
	* Place the heart of Marius (6-149) in the indentation in the torso’s chest.

Spirit of Marius Tricotor
* If all four of the correct symbolic objects are placed on the appropriate torsos, the spirit of Marius will return to possess the colossal head.
* It speaks in Mithric through the head’s mouth, starting with the following:
	* “I’m here. Why have you ripped me across the veil?”
* The spirit eschews the aristocratic tones favored by the previous magic mouth, and speaks Mithric in a common, even lower class, accent.  Marius is blunt and direct, caring nothing for niceties or circumlocutions.
* If treated politely, he is a font of potentially useful information and wisdom.
	* He can describe in detail the campaigns against the heqeti, as well as the characteristics and powers of the various heqeti types.
	* He has spirit-knowledge of the locations of the iconic objects attributed to him in the Lay of Marius Invictus (books), and can also provide directions to these locations, so long as the route passes through Archontean-era construction.
		* The ancient sky sled (the remaining ones are at 6-4, 6-100, and 7-36)
		* The iron circlet of Ghanor (3-127A)
		* The bone ring of Jagri-Naz (5-74)
		* The ebon spear (SL5-13B)
		* The tablet of the Beacon (9-107).
	* He can describe the original functions and layout of the Archontean areas (Levels 1, 2, 3, 4, parts of 5, parts of 6, and Sub-Levels 2, 3, 4, 6 and 7).
	* If asked about treasure, and if convinced it will be put to lawful purposes, he will reveal a hidden catch on the fourth platform that causes it to slide, revealing a short flight of stairs to a treasure vault.
		* 10 5-lb bars of platinum (1,250 gp each); an urn with 2,347 ancient silver pennies; a set of gold and emerald jewelry (necklace, earrings, and ring; total 5,000 gp); a suit of imperial field plate (av items); a rod of lordly might; a vorpal blade (long sword); a description of the troll thegn’s court (7-72 to 7-77) and his submission to Marius Tricotor. 
	* Marius’s spirit remains for 4-6 days.
		* At the end of that period, Marius cuts short any conversation with the following words: “Comrades, I’ve got to go. Carry yourself with honor and dignity, and always press the bastards when they least expect it. Look for me again after the full moon.”
		* He can be re-summoned after two months have passed.

8 stone legionaries, as Archontean animated constructs – spearmen (see new monsters): SZ M; AL N; AC 2; MV 60’; HD 6; HP 45, 42, 40, 39, 38, 37, 35, 33; #AT 1; Dmg 5-10; MR 25%. Special defenses: immune to elemental magic, poison, and mind-affecting spells; +1 or better weapons to hit; half damage from slashing or piercing weapons.

### 6-155: Lawful Propaganda Chamber

* This former meditation chamber has seen hard times, stripped of all furnishing.
	* A set of slogans (Mithric) is carved into the wall above now-destroyed frescoes.
		* Six slogans occupy the walls, one per 10’ section (except the section with the secret door).
			* Discipline makes one strong
			* Loyalty is its own reward
			* Death before dishonor
			* Order breeds happiness
			* Good lordship starts with good discipline
			* The Wise servant obeys without question
		* GM Note: the slogans obviously privilege principles of law over chaos. Although intended for general purposes by the Imperial authorities, they may also hint as to the alignment tendencies of the magic pool in 6-156.
	* Secret Door (north): easy to find (1 in 4), opens by pushing the ‘w’ of the word ‘wise’ in the sixth slogan (searching might detect wear around that letter).

### 6-156: Magic Pool

* The stairs and corridor lead to a pleasant, hemispherical chamber, whose walls and floor are tiled in pale green tiles.
	* A three-tiered fountain occupies almost all of the room, filled with bright yellow liquid that cascades invitingly down. 
	* The fountain is a magic pool. 
		* Drinking a draught provokes a roll on the following table; the results differ according to the drinker’s alignment:

D6
* LG, LE, LN
* NG, CG
* CN, True N
* NE, CE

1
* Cures 4-24 HP
* Cures 2-12 HP
* Cures 1-6 HP
* Inflicts 2-12 damage

2
* Restoration (at 15th level)
* Remove Curse
* Inflicts 1-6 damage
* Inflicts 1-6 damage

3
* Prot. From Chaos, 10’ radius, 6 hours
* Shield for 3-6 turns
* Infravision for 1-6 turns
* Penalty of 2 to AC for 1-3 days

4
* (+1 STR once only)
* +1 STR for 1-4 days
* Glow brightly for 1-6 days
* -1 STR (50% permanent, 50% for 1-4 days)

5
* (+1 CON once only)
* +1 CON for 1-4 days
* +1 to hit for 3-36 turns
* -1 STR (50% permanent, 50% for 1-4 days)

6
* Per potion of super-heroism for 2 days
* Per potion of heroism, for 2 days
* -1 to hit for 3-36 turns
* Opposite of potion of heroism (reducing levels) for 2 days; min. is level 1

### 6-157: Antechamber 

* This 20’-tall antechamber was the visitor's entry to the tomb of Marius Tricotor (6-154).
	* Four 12’-tall, half-round, granite carvings of legionaries are attached to the east and west walls, one each on either side of the east-west corridors.
	* The center of the room holds a 4’-tall, triangular dais made of striated marble.
		* In the center stands the spectral form of a legionary.
			* On entry, the legionary points north declaims slowly and loudly (Mithric):  “Seek the great Marius Tricotor down that corridor. Be prepared to offer him fealty, and he in turn will defend and protect you.”
			* Recent smears of blood are visible on the floor around the dais (the remains of the adventurers being devoured in 6-159).
	* The 10’-wide passage to the north is impassable due to an ancient cave-in.
		* GM: the only access the tomb of Marius Tricotor (6-154) the secret door in the ceiling of 6-145.
* Two bestial varumani are growling and pawing at the door to the south.
	* They attack any intruders on sight. More than four rounds of combat draws the other varumani in 6-159 and 6-160 to the fray, arriving on round 7.

2 bestial varumani (see new monsters): SZ L; AL NE; AC 4; MV 90’; HD 8; HP 58, 49; #AT 3; Dmg 3-6/3-6/3-10. Special defenses: regenerate 3 HP/rd; infravision; immune to poison.

### 6-158: Terrified Adventurer

* Lepp the thief hides in this former storeroom from the savage varumani who slew his comrades.
	* He has spiked the door shut, and is at wit’s end on how to escape.
* The chamber has built-in stone shelving, but almost everything was looted long ago.
	* All that remains are a stone jar of pickled beets on a top shelf.

Lepp, 5th-level male Wiskin thief: SZ M; AL NE; AC 5; MV 120’; HD 5; HP 8 (max 23); #AT 1; Dmg 3-6 (dagger +2), 1-6 (short sword). Abilities: STR 13, INT 15, WIS 9, DEX 17, CON 9, CHA 10. Thief skills: PP 55%, OL 52%, F/RT 40%, MS 45%, HS 36%, HN 20%, CW 90%, RL 25%. Possessions: leather armor; short sword; dagger +2; a potion of levitation; a purse with 129 gp, 57 sp, and a troll thegn’s passport (see Arden Vul items).

### 6-159: Renegade Varumani

* A band of 8 varumani who abandoned their fealty to the troll thegn makes its lair here.
	* Seven bestial, semi-intelligent varumani are led by a lesser varumani outcast, Bothig.
	* The reek of their lair is obvious from 30’ down the corridor.
* The chamber was once a pleasant, 20’-tall barrel-vaulted audience hall.
	* Bothig and his primitive followers have ruined any remnants of Mithric imagery.
	* Two piles of soft-ish trash serve as the trolls’ nests.
		* Bothig’s nest: 4,097 gp; 2,357 sp; 10 blue quartz gems (20 gp each); silver toe-ring (900 gp); silver and gold box (700 gp); silver and gems goblet (2,600 gp); silver and gold seal (200 gp), gold locket (800 gp).
	* The varumani are perpetually hungry, mostly surviving on small vermin from the caves north of 6-160.
		* They eagerly chase any intruders up to 6-136, but won’t enter the Troll Lift (6-5) or the domain of the frost mother (south of 6-136).
	* Bothig is capable of crude, but intelligible, speech, neither Bothig nor his friends have much interest in anything but rending and tearing. 
* Four varumani are currently devouring the bodies of four adventurers they slew in 6-157 and dragged here.  Two others are in 6-160 and two are in 6-157.
	* Adventurers’ gear: 349 sp; 211 gp; a heavy flail +1; banded mail +1; a set of four throwing axes +1; large shield +1, +4 vs. missiles; a pouch (77 gp of silvered sand); a tear of Kauket (new); a rod of turning (5 charges, new); a potion of the berserk (new); a short sword; a staff; damaged studded leather armor (still usable); and a scroll (sleep, telekinesis, project image).

Bothig, lesser varumani (see new monsters): SZ L; AL LE; AC 3; MV 90’; HD 8; HP 58; #AT 3 or 1; Dmg 3-6/3-6/4-10 or 7-22 (mace, 3-18+4). Special defenses: 33% resistant to mind-
affecting magic; immune to cold and poison; save as 8th-level fighter or 8th-level magic user, whichever is better; regenerate 3 HP/rd; infravision. Possessions: mace; shield.

3 bestial varumani (see new monsters): SZ L; AL NE; AC 4; MV 90’; HD 8; HP 55, 50, 49; #AT 3; Dmg 3-6/3-6/3-10. Special defenses: regenerate 3 HP/rd; infravision; immune to poison.

### 6-160: Ruined Dining Hall … with Varumani

* Two bestial varumani from Bothig’s band of renegades (6-159) wait on either side of the tunnel from 6-161 to ambush any prey that might emerge. 
* A 20’-long, heavy oaken table still stands in the center of the room, devoid of chairs.
	* A pile of bones (the past meals of the varumani) sits in the southwest corner.
	* The east wall bears a faded fresco in which Marius Tricotor, dressed in ordinary legionary armor, stands at the center of group of legionaries.
		* The caption reads (Mithric): “A great leader knows his men. Marius!”

2 bestial varumani (see new monsters): SZ L; AL NE; AC 4; MV 90’; HD 8; HP 55, 53; #AT 3; Dmg 3-6/3-6/3-10. Special defenses: regenerate 3 HP/rd; infravision; immune to poison.

### 6-161: Pleasant Cave

* This large cave is humid and warm, with a species of green lichen emiting pale green phosphorescence, and numerous cave crickets and small lizards.
	* The southwestern lobe of the cave contains a pool of cool, clear water.
	* The 6' wide northern tunnel exits the cave about 10’ up the wall.
	* The southern tunnel is 20’ up the cave wall, and only 3’ wide. 
* Anyone resting here for more than 1d3 hours will be visited by a gray ooze from 6-165. 

1 gray ooze (after 1-3 hours): SZ L; AL N; AC 8; MV 10’; HD 3+3; HP 23; #AT 1; Dmg 2-16. Special attacks: corrode metal. Special defenses: impervious to spells; immune to heat and cold. 

##### 6-161a: Tunnel leading up to SL12-13

* 5’ above the floor on the western wall of 6-161 is a perfectly round, perfectly smooth tunnel leading upwards in wide spirals to SL12-13.
	* It was bored by Kerbog Khan’s borer automaton (see SL12-19).
	* The slope of the passage is just gentle enough to allow bipeds to traverse it without slipping (+3x difficult terrain or risk slipping).

### 6-162: Rudishva Transport Hall

* The iris door to 6-163 opens to pale green, pink, orange, silver, or yellow rudishva identity plaques. 
* This ancient rudishva hall has no right angles, and is sheathed in hexagonal white tiles.
	* Most of the chamber is taken up by a 15’-diameter, 3’-deep black granite fountain.
		* The liquid in the fountain is opalescent and sparkly. Anything (or anyone) coated in the liquid can levitate in the shaft (6-164). 
	* Teleport Nodes 
		* Silvery disks on the floor and a silvery square inset on the wall. Touching the square teleport one on the pad to the appropriate location.
		* T14: access to 5-31
		* T16: access to 7-6 (floating garden)

### 6-163: Giant Rudishva Skeletal Guardians

* The door to 6-162 is one of the rudishva iris doors, and only opens by presenting a pale green, pink, orange, silver, or yellow rudishva identity plaque (see new technological items). 
* This 15’-tall chamber is sheathed in hexagonal white tiles, with no right angles.
	* Two granite chairs occupy the center of the room, angled so both face the entry point from 6-164.  Each chair holds a giant rudishva skeleton.
		* Anyone exiting the transit shaft (6-164) is met with a harsh challange (rudishva), and mercilessly attacked if they don't immediately present a pale green, orange, pink or silver rudishva identity plaque.
	* An 8’-square hole in the west wall provides access to the transit shaft.

2 semi-intelligent giant rudishva skeletons: SZ L; AL NE; AC 2; MV 90’; HD 8+8; HP 68, 55; #AT 1 or 2; Dmg 3-18 (weapon) or 2-8/2-8 (bone throwing); MR 50%. Special attacks: bone 
throwing; sonic blast. Special defenses: +1 or better weapons to hit; half damage from sharp or edged weapons; half damage from fire; immune to sleep, charm, cold, poison, and paralysis.

### 6-164: Transit shaft, with Impaled Dwarf

* A 40’-square shaft, sheathed in white marble and silver grout, extends 1,100’ through the Halls, commencing at 5-84 and culminating at 9-91 (~500' below).
	* Built  as swift transport for rudishva officers, it detects as strongly magical.
	* Things coated in the opalescent liquid is capable of levitation in the pit (20' / round).
	* Removal of even 10% of the silver grout cancels the levitation effect.
	* From this point one can use the shaft to access 5-84, 7-146 and 9-91.
	* The opening to 6-163 is obvious and easily accessible to those traversing the shaft. 
* The body of a dwarf is impaled against the east wall of the chasm by monstrous femurs.
	* A victim of the giant rudishva skeletons at 6-163.
	* Dwarf-sized chain mail, battle axe +1, 50’ coil of rope, 10 spikes, a potion of healing, an inert dwarven life-stone from the clan Goethite, sack full of desiccated bits of fruit.

### 6-165: Ooze Chamber with Pukel-mander

* The northern and eastern of the chamber are worked in the heqeti manner, with pebbled, oily walls. 
	* An enormous gray ooze typically inhabits the southern, natural lobe of the cave.
		* If encountered in 6-161, it might not be here. 
	* To the east, down the partly finished corridor, a pukel-mander (new) looms over the cave at 6-166. 
* The central feature of the cave is an enormous pool of roiling and burping slimes of different colors and consistencies.
	* The slime pit is about 10’ deep and roughly 20’ in diameter, filled with several noxious slimes extruded by Rimmaq-Isfet itself and imported from the Abyss.
	* Unlike the comparable pool at 5-104, this one never produced the right combination of slimes for the attack on the rudishva, and the heqeti abandoned it. 
	* At any given time 4 heqeti slimes are visible on the surface of the pool.
		* Every hour of waiting, 75% chance one slime will submerge and 1d2 new ones will rise to the surface. 

1 electric blue, liquid but adhesive heqeti slime (see new monsters): SZ S; AL N; AC 6; MV 5’ creeping; HD 2; HP 10; #AT 1; Dmg special; MR 15%. Special attacks: touch causes painful 
boils for 1-3 days followed by death; infectious. Special defenses: healed by electricity and lasers; slowed by cold.

1 rainbow, oily and thick heqeti slime (see new monsters): SZ S; AL N; AC 6; MV 10’ creeping; HD 2; HP 11; #AT 1; Dmg special; MR 15%. Special attacks: changes 25% of epidermis per 
hit to thick yellow fur. Special defenses: healed by electricity and lasers; slowed by cold.

1 blue-black, gluey heqeti slime (see new monsters): SZ S; AL N; AC 6; MV 15’ pseudopod; HD 2; HP 12; #AT 1; Dmg 1-6; MR 15%. Special attacks: flesh-eating for 4-7 rounds. Special 
defenses: healed by electricity and lasers; slowed by cold.

1 sickly-green, oily and runny heqeti slime (see new monsters): SZ S; AL N; AC 6; MV 20’ on liquids; HD 2; HP 13; #AT 1; Dmg special; MR 15%. Special attacks: flesh animating (covers 
flesh and kills victim in 4-7 rounds, then re-animates as a heqeti slime zombie - see new monsters); corrosive to metal. Special defenses: healed by electricity and lasers; slowed by cold.

1 gray ooze: SZ L; AL N; AC 8; MV 10’; HD 3+3; HP 23; #AT 1; Dmg 2-16. Special attacks: corrode metal. Special defenses: impervious to spells; immune to heat and cold. 

### 6-166: Crossroads Cave, with tunnels to 5-100, SL6-56, and the Chasm (6-108)

* Stalactites and stalagmites dot this 30’-tall cavern.
	* A tunnel to the northwest slopes upward to 5-100.
	* One to the east slopes gently down to the Great Chasm (6-108).
	* A third tunnel, difficult to locate and only 3’ in diameter, is near the ceiling of the northeast wall; it leads up to SL6-56 of the Drowned Canyon.
* At the west end of the cave is a ledge containing a heqeti pukel-mander (see 6-165).
	* At the foot of the ledge is the corpse of a human magic user.
		* Belt pouch (55 pp, 43 gp, 39 sp), a bone scroll case with scrolls (secret chest and levitation).
		* Spell Book: Alarm, armor, burning hands, firewater, grease, read magic, taunt; deeppockets, irritation, preserve, vocalize, zephyr; cloudburst, item, monster summoning I; ultravision.

### 6-167: Cave of Gimon
 
* This small cave is the abode of the strange creature known as Gimon (new).
* Gimon abides here (present 50%), in a surprisingly well-kept cave.
	* On a ledge in the back of the cave is the idol of Camazotz (new).
	* Next to it is a forgotten purse with 10 impressive pearls (120 gp each).

Gimon (see new monsters): SZ M; AL N; AC 7; MV 60’, 150’ flying (Class D); HD 6; HP 40; #AT 3; Dmg 1-4/1-4/1-6; MR 25%. Special defenses: cannot be surprised; immune to cold.
* Gimon was a human adventurer who found the potent idol of Camazotz (new) and fell under its spell. After several months of possessing it, he transformed into a bat creature.
* He is bipedal, quite skinny, with arms connected to his body with bat wings and  impressive fangs.
* Despite his monstrous appearance, Gimon is not evil; he is probably insane, though.
	* He flies about the middle levels of Great Chasm, feeding on other predators and occasionally rescuing the weak.
	* The workers at the Troll Lifts know him well and don’t bother him; refering to him, rather fondly, as the ‘Bat-monk’.  Despite their neutrality, Gimon is too skittish to form friendships with them.
* He will likely hear intruders before they enter his cave, and takes flight to avoid being trapped in his cave.
* As long as the idol of Camazotz remains untouched, he will not bother those who ransack his cave (although they will not be beneficiaries of his ‘rescue missions’).
	* He will pursue to the death anyone who carries off his idol.

### 6-168: Two-lobed Cave

* The front of this cave opens onto the chasm.  It is nondescript rock and the occasional home of chasm cephalopods (25% chance).
	* At the back is a narrow crack, 2’ wide and 4’ tall, leading to a second, larger cave.
* This section is drier, sandier and a fine place to rest without fear of attack.
	* Gimon knows of this cave and might recommend it to those whom he trusts.

4 medium chasm cephalopods (see new monsters) (25% chance): SZ M; AL N; AC 5; MV 60’ flying (Class A); HD 4; HP 27, 26, 25, 24; #AT 5 (4 tentacles and a beak); Dmg 1-4/1-4/1-
4/1-4/1-6; MR 25%. Special attacks: surprise on 1-4.
